This is the best food joint in Ramona!! Hands down some of the best food. they cover every need, from deli sandwiches and burgers for a quick lunch bite, to all things sushi. And Mr. Tuna(Ken)cuts sushi like no other! His dishes look like what you see on a TV show! Sam my waiter was amazing! My drinks never hit the bottom! Everyone here is just cool. Even the cook Hoss has a bomb burger on the menu. They make the vibe here perfect! This pick is the "big O fish" sandwich! Ahi tuna with soft shell crab! It is a must try! From bomb beer selections to sake and wine. What are you waiting for? Go!!!< /text>

< Review>
This has been the local "starbucks" long before Starbucks owner was most likely born. Lol The local hollypark veterans go there and talk about sports, news, local info for over 40 years. I have childhood memories of my grandfather walking us here with our saved up pennies to cash them in for donut holes and cola in the glass bottle. They are remodeling the entire corner after 35 years. Change is good but I wonder what took it so long. Donut hold come free now with the purchase of one donut ranging from $1 and up. Wish I would have saved my pennies. Lol< /Review>

We camped here in our fifth wheel a few weeks ago. It was a Sunday and really crowded.  We were half an hour early before check in so we needed to just wait. We saw a sign that said RV parking only. No vehicles. Perfect! A place we could hang out and wait. I jumped out to get food. Soon after my husband called and said he had to move the RV. I walked over from the cafe to see if our spot was open and it was, so I texted him to drive over to our spot. As I was helping my husband back in the RV, a woman walked up to me and pointed her finger at me and sternly said, ‚ÄúYOUR HUSBAND PARKED IN SOMEONE ELSE‚ÄôS SPOT!‚Äù Confused, I replied, ‚Äúwhat‚Äù?  She repeated the same thing, pointing at him and then pointing back at me for some reason. I said, ‚Äúwho are you?‚Äù She said she was the camp host. I was so confused because I had no idea what she was talking about. I explained there was a sign that said RV parking, and we were just waiting 30 min. for check in.  (See picture) It doesn‚Äôt say campsites. She didn‚Äôt care and said, ‚ÄúAt least you actually do have a reservation because most people lie about that too!! So obviously you have never stayed with us , so let‚Äôs go over the rules!!‚Äù  She didn‚Äôt introduce herself when she walked up to me, just pointed her finger and yelled, was never friendly, and talked down to us the whole time. I‚Äôm pretty sure her name was Beverly. Then, the next morning at 5 am traffic began, since the RV spots are actually on the road, you hear everyone driving to work. We will never camp there again.< /Text>

<Text>I love this town and beach!  We are locals, lived here in SLO County from birth. We have always wanted to camp by the ocean in Avila but have never been able to get in. We have managed to stay at the RV camping up on the bluff. So, I was so excited when I managed to get a site at the Nobi area! Campsite #5 was the only site I could find available. For 4 nights!  Not over the weekend, but we were super happy to get one at all. The day we were leaving to come camp I checked the website and found out that Nobi 3 was available for two of the 4 nights we were there!  If you‚Äôve been to Nobi, you know that site 5 is directly behind 3 and a camper in 3 can pretty much totally block site 5‚Äôs view of the ocean. Well, it was too late to cancel our original reservation without full penalty. But to us, it was worth it to pay for both sites to be able to have the unobstructed view of the ocean for two of the days.  I quickly reserved #3 and we were on our way. We stayed the first night with a small motor home between us and the ocean. The second night, the view was ours and we enjoyed it immensely. On the 3rd day the camp host texted me and asked when we were coming in. I responded that we were there already, parked in space 5. A few minutes later the camp hosts drove up, we had an issue and that we could not occupy 2 spaces unless we had another camper in the other one. We explained what happened. Their only response was, see the port for reimbursement.  We‚Äôll we didn‚Äôt mind losing the money, especially if we had unknowingly broken the rules. The next day a huge Tiffan motor home with a full size Jeep pulled in, right in front of us. Gone was all of our view.  We were so disappointed. If we‚Äôd known the hosts were going to cancel one of reservations for that day, we would have chooses to move into the view site. But we had been told nothing about opening one of the sites we paid for to another camper.  My husband went to talk to the office the next day. They basically said, tough, you broke the rule, it‚Äôs too popular here for someone to have two sites and not occupy both. No refund. We ended up enjoying some days and hours with the spot in front of us empty. But the whole experience with the hosts was so negative it took a lot of joy out of our vacation. I got an ant infestation in my RV that lasted a month. I had to take it to a place to put a tarp over it and exhumed it. <UserId.>115336611467996143175< /UserId.><Name>Martha Locke</Name>< Date>
1619313148988<//Date>
< Rate>
4</Rate>
< Text>
Decent campground, decent price, lovely setting.

Pros:
- Lots of trees; an actual campground type setting (not a parking lot)
- Significantly less expensive than the privately owned campgrounds nearby
- Accepts reservations
- Quiet/peaceful
- People staying in the campground are generally friendly
- Dogs allowed
- Camp sites each have a table, fire pit, and a BBQ (bring your coals!!)

Cons:
- Not near the beach or downtown
- Campsites are right on top of each other, so you hear and see everything the neighbors are saying & doing, and kids have no place to play without being in another camper's space
- Overzealous park rangers (caretakers?) - we were told we couldn't run our RV's heater overnight because of it being outside of allowed generator hours. (No, we weren't running the RV's generator or engine.)
- Reservations are site specific, and no site switching is permitted after check-in, even if the site is empty/unreserved.
- Drive-throughs not allowed, to check it out before you reserve. (This*may* be Covid related)

Overall decent experience, just be sure going in that you are ready to be patient with the other campers, as it's frequently full to capacity (and that means you'll have very little wiggle room).< /Text>

< text>
We camped here in June, 2 years ago. This is one of my favorite camp ground and it is great for biking, hiking, bird watching, walking on the beach. The Museum is just across the street. There are also a lot of restaurants and shops nearby, just a mile away from the camp. Facilities are well maintained. They have private bathroom and showers. Showers need token though. One token is 2 min each. Each camp is spacious has picnic table and chairs, camp fire bins and barbecue grill. During the night, it is really cold and you can hear the waves crushing to the rocks.<//text>

< text>
It's OK in a pinch.

Cons: Noisy, crowded, smokey, very small spaces, nearby electronic foghorn sounds all night. The "fire rings" are like half-height barrels and ruin any campfire experience because you can't really see the fire. If you're used to clamping in nice spots, Morro Bay SP Campground is sure to disappoint.

Pros: Very nice bathrooms with flush toilets,  convenient to nearby sights.< /text>

<time>1528985965086</time><Rating>5<//Rating>< text>
We love tent camping here.  There are lots of trees and a great view of the estuary and mountains.   We use the fire pit to cook or just sit by at night.  Fire wood sold at the campgrounds.  Bring along a couple of chairs for sitting by the fire. Bathrooms are available and cleaned daily.  Showers take tokens.  Peaceful atmosphere where everyone quiets down by 10pm.
Restaurant, museum and beaches nearby.  Going into Morro Bay for fresh fish to cook at the campsite is a treat.  Cambria is about 20 minutes away.</text>

< text>
Morro Bay State Park has been my favorite campground for sixty years   My dad introduced us to the park when I was eight years old.  Over the years the campground has gotten run down, bathrooms and showers closed due to needed repairs, and those that are open are deplorable, sharing your showers with ants, spiders, mold, doors that won't lock,  and occasionally cold water.  At $38.50 - 50.00 a night it should be better, but unfortunately the powers that be have decided to continue to let the park go downhill.  The hookups are generally always full, and the rest if the park is too in the summer.  I am wondering where the money is going, certainly not being put back in this campground.< /text>

<review>Pretty good campground, although fairly open.  The staff were quite helpful, and regularly made rounds to clean the washrooms which is much appreciated.  Not as nice as some of the campgrounds we've stayed in (you need to take your own soap or hand sanitizer to the washroom) but overall pretty clean.  Fire pits and picnic tables on each site were well used but nice and solid.  Lots of owl activity at night, and birds during the day with a few monarch butterflies flitting through and with it being not too far from the beach it was a nice escape to nature for the weekend. <Rating>4<//Rating><time>1522120103159<//time><Resp>None< /Resp><Review>It can be very crowded and tightly packed with noisy, unsupervised younglings, but it always has some stunning vistas.
It can be quite chilly waiting for the campgrounds shower water to warm up, but if you thought ahead and brought more than enough shower tokens into the shower room with you, that shower can be renewing.
Now, regarding proximity, this Park is very conveniently placed within a short drive to a whole lotta good places to visit: Morro Rock, the MB Embarcadero, to Los Osos and the Grocery Outlet there, to an indoor theater in MB, and to a drive-in theater in San Luis Obispo, to The Brickhouse BBQ restaurant on Main St. in MB, to Albertsons grocery store, to Morro Bay Propane & Moving, and to the Mobil Station on MB Blvd. for good prices on 22oz. craft beers.
But whatever you do while here, don't pass up your opportunity to rent a kayak at the marina across from the park. It's inexpensive, low impact, easy rowing exercise that even old people can enjoy. </record></dataset><record>
<Resp>None< /Resp>< text>
Right across street from a harbor and next to a golf course. Very nice "suburban" campground. Worth the price because of the location about three miles away from the downtown Morro Bay area. A trolley runs there in the summer (starts roughly late May / Memorial Day) park has wifi, works decently when I tested it. Not a ton of privacy and mostly frequented by RVers. Some tent sites have shade, otherwise sites are in rows out in the open. Some sites have views of harbor. Yeah it's expensive but the people with the $200K RVs don't seem to mind, I suspect this campground is generally free of rowdies and homeless types because of / justifying the cost. The presence of CA State Park law enforcement types keeps this and Montana D Oro relatively pest free :)<//text>
